<p>The <b>House of Bourbon</b> (<span class="nowrap"><small>English</small> <span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ɔːr/ 'or' in 'abhor'">ɔːr</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ən/ 'on' in 'button'">ən</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <small>French: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_French" title="Help:IPA for French">[buʁˈbɔ̃]</a></span>) is a European <a href="/wiki/Dynasty" title="Dynasty">royal house</a> of French origin, a branch of the <a href="/wiki/Capetian_dynasty" title="Capetian dynasty">Capetian dynasty</a> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/iː/ long 'e' in 'seed'">iː</span><span title="/ʃ/ 'sh' in 'shy'">ʃ</span><span title="/ən/ 'on' in 'button'">ən</span></span>/</a></span></span>). Bourbon kings first ruled France and <a href="/wiki/Navarre" title="Navarre">Navarre</a> in the 16th century. By the 18th century, members of the Bourbon dynasty also held thrones in Spain, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Naples" title="Kingdom of Naples">Naples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Two_Sicilies" title="Kingdom of the Two Sicilies">Sicily</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Parma" title="Duchy of Parma">Parma</a>. Spain and Luxembourg currently have Bourbon monarchs.</p>
<p>The royal Bourbons originated in 1268, when the heiress of the <a href="/wiki/Sire_de_Bourbon" title="Sire de Bourbon">lordship of Bourbon</a> married a younger son of King <a href="/wiki/Louis_IX_of_France" title="Louis IX of France">Louis IX</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anselme_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-anselme-1">[1]</a></sup> The house continued for three centuries as a <a href="/wiki/Cadet_branch" title="Cadet branch">cadet branch</a>, while more senior Capetians ruled France, until <a href="/wiki/Henry_IV_of_France" title="Henry IV of France">Henry IV</a> became the first Bourbon king of France in 1589.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anselme_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-anselme-1">[1]</a></sup> Bourbon monarchs then unified France with the small <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Navarre" title="Kingdom of Navarre">kingdom of Navarre</a>, which Henry's father had acquired by marriage in 1555, and ruled until the 1792 overthrow of the monarchy during the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>. Restored briefly in 1814 and definitively in 1815 after the fall of the <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">First French Empire</a>, the senior line of the Bourbons was finally overthrown in the <a href="/wiki/July_Revolution" title="July Revolution">July Revolution</a> of 1830. A cadet Bourbon branch, the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Orl%C3%A9ans" title="House of Orléans">House of Orléans</a>, then ruled for 18 years (1830–1848), until it too was overthrown.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Princes_of_Cond%C3%A9" title="Princes of Condé">Princes de Condé</a> were a cadet branch of the Bourbons descended from an uncle of Henry IV, and the <a href="/wiki/Princes_of_Conti" title="Princes of Conti">Princes de Conti</a> were a cadet branch of the Condé. Both houses were prominent in French affairs, even during exile in the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>, until their respective extinctions in 1830 and 1814.</p>
<p>When the Bourbons inherited the strongest claim to the Spanish throne, the claim was passed to a <a href="/wiki/Cadet_(genealogy)" title="Cadet (genealogy)">cadet</a> Bourbon prince, a grandson of <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV_of_France" title="Louis XIV of France">Louis XIV of France</a>, who became <a href="/wiki/Philip_V_of_Spain" title="Philip V of Spain">Philip V of Spain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anselme_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-anselme-1">[1]</a></sup> Permanent separation of the French and Spanish thrones was secured when France and Spain <a href="/wiki/Ratification" title="Ratification">ratified</a> Philip's <a href="/wiki/Renunciation" title="Renunciation">renunciation</a>, for himself and his descendants, of the French throne in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Utrecht" title="Treaty of Utrecht">Treaty of Utrecht</a> in 1714, and similar arrangements later kept the Spanish throne separate from those of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Two_Sicilies" title="Kingdom of the Two Sicilies">the Two Sicilies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Parma" title="Duchy of Parma">Parma</a>. The Spanish House of Bourbon (rendered in Spanish as <i>Borbón</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Spanish" title="Help:IPA for Spanish">[borˈβon]</a></span>) has been overthrown and restored several times, reigning 1700–1808, 1813–1868, 1875–1931, and since 1975. Bourbons ruled in <a href="/wiki/List_of_monarchs_of_Naples" title="List of monarchs of Naples">Naples</a> from 1734–1806 and in <a href="/wiki/List_of_monarchs_of_Sicily" title="List of monarchs of Sicily">Sicily</a> from 1734–1816, and in a unified <a href="/wiki/List_of_monarchs_of_the_Kingdom_of_the_Two_Sicilies" title="List of monarchs of the Kingdom of the Two Sicilies">Kingdom of the Two Sicilies</a> from 1816–1860. They also ruled in <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Parma" title="Duke of Parma">Parma</a> from 1731–1735, 1748–1802 and 1847–1859.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_Grand_Duchess_of_Luxembourg" title="Charlotte, Grand Duchess of Luxembourg">Charlotte, Grand Duchess of Luxembourg</a> married a cadet of the Parmese line and thus her successors, who have ruled Luxembourg since her abdication in 1964, have also been members of the House of Bourbon. <a href="/wiki/Isabel,_Princess_Imperial_of_Brazil" title="Isabel, Princess Imperial of Brazil">Isabel, Princess Imperial of Brazil</a>, regent for her father, <a href="/wiki/Pedro_II_of_Brazil" title="Pedro II of Brazil">Pedro II</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Empire of Brazil</a>, married a cadet of the Orléans line and thus their descendants, known as the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Imperial_Family" title="Brazilian Imperial Family">Orléans-Braganza</a>, were in the <a href="/wiki/Line_of_succession_to_the_former_Brazilian_throne" title="Line of succession to the former Brazilian throne">line of succession to the Brazilian throne</a> and expected to ascend its throne had the monarchy not been abolished by revolution in 1889.</p>
<p>All legitimate, living members of the House of Bourbon, including its cadet branches, are direct <a href="/wiki/Primogeniture#Agnatic_primogeniture" title="Primogeniture">agnatic descendants</a> of Henry IV.</p>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chateau_de_Bourbon_l%27Archambault_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Chateau_de_Bourbon_l%27Archambault_01.jpg/220px-Chateau_de_Bourbon_l%27Archambault_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Chateau_de_Bourbon_l%27Archambault_01.jpg/330px-Chateau_de_Bourbon_l%27Archambault_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Chateau_de_Bourbon_l%27Archambault_01.jpg/440px-Chateau_de_Bourbon_l%27Archambault_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chateau_de_Bourbon_l%27Archambault_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The castle of <a href="/wiki/Bourbon-l%27Archambault" title="Bourbon-l'Archambault">Bourbon-l'Archambault</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The pre-Capetian House of <a href="/wiki/Bourbonnais" title="Bourbonnais">Bourbon</a> was a <a href="/wiki/Nobility" title="Nobility">noble</a> family, dating at least from the beginning of the 13th century, when the <a href="/wiki/Family_seat" title="Family seat">estate</a> of Bourbon was ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Sire_de_Bourbon" title="Sire de Bourbon">Sire de Bourbon</a> who was a vassal of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_of_France" title="King of France">King of France</a>. The term House of Bourbon ("Maison de Bourbon") is sometimes used to refer to this <a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Premi%C3%A8re_maison_de_Bourbon" title="fr:Première maison de Bourbon">first house</a> and the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bourbon-Dampierre" title="House of Bourbon-Dampierre">House of Bourbon-Dampierre</a>, the second family to rule the <a href="/wiki/Manorialism" title="Manorialism">seigneury</a>.</p>
<p>In 1268, <a href="/wiki/Robert,_Count_of_Clermont" title="Robert, Count of Clermont">Robert, Count of Clermont</a>, sixth son of King <a href="/wiki/Louis_IX_of_France" title="Louis IX of France">Louis IX of France</a>, married <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beatrix_of_Burgundy,_Dame_de_Bourbon" title="Beatrix of Burgundy, Dame de Bourbon">Beatrix of Bourbon</a>, heiress to the <a href="/wiki/Sire_de_Bourbon" title="Sire de Bourbon">lordship of Bourbon</a> and member of the House of Bourbon-Dampierre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anselme_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-anselme-1">[1]</a></sup> Their son <a href="/wiki/Louis_I,_Duke_of_Bourbon" title="Louis I, Duke of Bourbon">Louis</a> was made <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Bourbon" title="Duke of Bourbon">Duke of Bourbon</a> in 1327. His descendant, the <a href="/wiki/Constable_of_France" title="Constable of France">Constable of France</a> <a href="/wiki/Charles_III,_Duke_of_Bourbon" title="Charles III, Duke of Bourbon">Charles de Bourbon</a>, was the last of the senior Bourbon line when he died in 1527. Because he chose to fight under the banner of <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V</a> and lived in exile from France, his title was discontinued after his death.</p>
<p>The remaining line of Bourbons henceforth descended from <a href="/wiki/James_I,_Count_of_La_Marche" title="James I, Count of La Marche">James I, Count of La Marche</a>, the younger son of <a href="/wiki/Louis_I,_Duke_of_Bourbon" title="Louis I, Duke of Bourbon">Louis I, Duke of Bourbon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anselme_1-4"><a href="#cite_note-anselme-1">[1]</a></sup> With the death of his grandson <a href="/wiki/James_II,_Count_of_La_Marche" title="James II, Count of La Marche">James II, Count of La Marche</a> in 1438, the senior line of the Count of La Marche became extinct. All future Bourbons would descend from James II's younger brother, <a href="/wiki/Louis,_Count_of_Vend%C3%B4me" title="Louis, Count of Vendôme">Louis</a>, who became the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Count_of_Vend%C3%B4me" title="Count of Vendôme">Count of Vendôme</a> through his mother's inheritance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anselme_1-5"><a href="#cite_note-anselme-1">[1]</a></sup> While the most senior branch of the family, the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Valois" title="House of Valois">House of Valois</a>, continued to occupy the throne of France, at the death of <a href="/wiki/Charles_IV,_Duke_of_Alen%C3%A7on" title="Charles IV, Duke of Alençon">Charles IV, Duke of Alençon</a> in 1525, all of the <a href="/wiki/Prince_du_sang" title="Prince du sang">princes of the blood royal</a> were Bourbons.</p>
<p>In 1514, <a href="/wiki/Charles,_Duke_of_Vend%C3%B4me" title="Charles, Duke of Vendôme">Charles, Count of Vendôme</a> had his title raised to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duke_of_Vend%C3%B4me" title="Duke of Vendôme">Duke of Vendôme</a>. His son <a href="/wiki/Antoine_of_Navarre" title="Antoine of Navarre">Antoine</a> became King of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Navarre" title="Kingdom of Navarre">Navarre</a>, on the northern side of the <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenees</a>, by marriage in 1555.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anselme_1-6"><a href="#cite_note-anselme-1">[1]</a></sup> Two of Antoine's younger brothers were Cardinal Archbishop <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Bourbon_(cardinal)" title="Charles de Bourbon (cardinal)">Charles de Bourbon</a> and the French and Huguenot general <a href="/wiki/Louis,_Prince_of_Cond%C3%A9_(1530%E2%80%931569)" title="Louis, Prince of Condé (1530–1569)">Louis de Bourbon, 1st Prince of Condé</a>. Louis' male-line, the <a href="/wiki/Princes_of_Cond%C3%A9" title="Princes of Condé">Princes de Condé</a>, survived until 1830. Finally, in 1589, the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Valois" title="House of Valois">House of Valois</a> died out and Antoine's son <a href="/wiki/Henry_IV_of_France" title="Henry IV of France">Henry III of Navarre</a> became Henry IV of France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anselme_1-7"><a href="#cite_note-anselme-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_Bourbons">List of Bourbons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Bourbon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: List of Bourbons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="France">France</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Bourbon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: France">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rise_of_Henry_IV">Rise of Henry IV</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Bourbon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Rise of Henry IV">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Henry_IV_of_France%27s_succession" title="Henry IV of France's succession">Henry IV of France's succession</a></div>
<p>The first Bourbon <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_of_France" title="King of France">king of France</a> was <a href="/wiki/Henry_IV_of_France" title="Henry IV of France">Henry IV</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anselme_1-8"><a href="#cite_note-anselme-1">[1]</a></sup> He was born on 13 December 1553 in the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Navarre" title="Kingdom of Navarre">Kingdom of Navarre</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antoine_de_Bourbon" title="Antoine de Bourbon">Antoine de Bourbon</a>, his father, was a ninth-generation descendant of King <a href="/wiki/Louis_IX_of_France" title="Louis IX of France">Louis IX of France</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anselme_1-9"><a href="#cite_note-anselme-1">[1]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jeanne_d%27Albret" title="Jeanne d'Albret">Jeanne d'Albret</a>, his mother was the Queen of Navarre and niece of King <a href="/wiki/Francis_I_of_France" title="Francis I of France">Francis I of France</a>. He was baptized <a href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">Catholic</a>, but raised <a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Calvinist</a>. After his father was killed in 1562, he became <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duke_of_Vend%C3%B4me" title="Duke of Vendôme">Duke of Vendôme</a> at the age of 10, with Admiral <a href="/wiki/Gaspard_II_de_Coligny" title="Gaspard II de Coligny">Gaspard de Coligny</a> (1519–1572) as his regent. Seven years later, the young duke became the nominal leader of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huguenots" title="Huguenots">Huguenots</a> after the death of his uncle the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis_I,_Prince_of_Cond%C3%A9" title="Louis I, Prince of Condé">Prince de Condé</a> in 1569.</p>
<p>Henry succeeded to Navarre as Henry III when his mother died in 1572. That same year <a href="/wiki/Catherine_de%27_Medici" title="Catherine de' Medici">Catherine de' Medici</a>, mother of King <a href="/wiki/Charles_IX_of_France" title="Charles IX of France">Charles IX of France</a>, arranged for the marriage of her daughter, <a href="/wiki/Margaret_of_Valois" title="Margaret of Valois">Margaret of Valois</a>, to Henry, ostensibly to advance peace between Catholics and Huguenots. Many Huguenots gathered in Paris for the wedding on 24 August, but were ambushed and slaughtered by Catholics in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Bartholomew%27s_Day_Massacre" title="St. Bartholomew's Day Massacre">St. Bartholomew's Day Massacre</a>. Henry saved his own life by converting to Catholicism. He repudiated his conversion in 1576 and resumed his leadership of the Huguenots.</p>
<p>The period from 1576 to 1584 was relatively calm in France, with the Huguenots consolidating control of much of the south with only occasional interference from the royal government. Extended civil war erupted again in 1584, when <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois,_Duke_of_Anjou" title="François, Duke of Anjou">François, Duke of Anjou</a>, younger brother of King <a href="/wiki/Henry_III_of_France" title="Henry III of France">Henry III of France</a>, died, leaving Navarre next in line for the throne. Thus began the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Three_Henrys" title="War of the Three Henrys">War of the Three Henrys</a>, as Henry of Navarre, Henry III, and the ultra-Catholic leader, <a href="/wiki/Henry_I,_Duke_of_Guise" title="Henry I, Duke of Guise">Henry of Guise</a>, fought a confusing three-cornered struggle for dominance. After Henry III was assassinated on 31 July 1589, Navarre claimed the throne as the first Bourbon king of France, Henry IV.</p>
<p>Much of Catholic France, organized into the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_League_(French)" title="Catholic League (French)">Catholic League</a>, refused to recognize a Protestant monarch and instead recognized Henry IV's uncle, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles,_Cardinal_de_Bourbon" title="Charles, Cardinal de Bourbon">Charles, Cardinal de Bourbon</a>, as rightful king, and the civil war continued. Henry won a crucial victory at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ivry" title="Battle of Ivry">Ivry</a> on 14 March 1590 and, following the death of the Cardinal the same year, the forces of the League lacked an obvious Catholic candidate for the throne and divided into various factions. Nevertheless, as a Protestant, Henry IV was unable to take Paris, a Catholic stronghold, or to decisively defeat his enemies, now supported by the Spanish. He reconverted to Catholicism in 1593—he is said to have remarked, "Paris is well worth a mass"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup>—and was crowned king retroactively to 1589 at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Chartres" title="Cathedral of Chartres">Cathedral of Chartres</a> on 27 February 1594.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Bourbons_in_France">Early Bourbons in France</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Bourbon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Early Bourbons in France">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Henry granted the <a href="/wiki/Edict_of_Nantes" title="Edict of Nantes">Edict of Nantes</a> on 13 April 1598, establishing Catholicism as an official state religion but also granting the Huguenots a measure of religious tolerance and political freedom short of full equality with the practice of Catholicism. This compromise ended the religious wars in France. That same year the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Vervins" title="Treaty of Vervins">Treaty of Vervins</a> ended the war with Spain, adjusted the Spanish-French border, and resulted in a belated recognition by Spain of Henry as king of France.</p>
<p>Ably assisted by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maximilien_de_B%C3%A9thune,_duc_de_Sully" title="Maximilien de Béthune, duc de Sully">Maximilien de Béthune, duc de Sully</a>, Henry reduced the land tax known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Taille" title="Taille">taille</a></i>; promoted agriculture, public works, construction of highways, and the first French canal; started such important industries as the tapestry works of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gobelins_manufactory" title="Gobelins manufactory">Gobelins</a>; and intervened in favor of Protestants in the duchies and earldoms along the German frontier. This last was to be the cause of his assassination.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Henry_IV_of_france_by_pourbous_younger.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="634" height="284" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Henry_IV_of_france_by_pourbous_younger.jpg/180px-Henry_IV_of_france_by_pourbous_younger.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Henry_IV_of_france_by_pourbous_younger.jpg/270px-Henry_IV_of_france_by_pourbous_younger.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Henry_IV_of_france_by_pourbous_younger.jpg/360px-Henry_IV_of_france_by_pourbous_younger.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Henry_IV_of_france_by_pourbous_younger.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Henry IV of France, the first Bourbon King of France</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Henry's marriage to Margaret, which had produced no heir, was annulled in 1599 and he married <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marie_de_Medici" title="Marie de Medici">Marie de Medici</a>, niece of the grand duke of Tuscany. A son, Louis, was born to them in 1601. Henry IV was assassinated on 14 May 1610 in Paris. <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIII_of_France" title="Louis XIII of France">Louis XIII</a> was only nine years old when he succeeded his father.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anselme_1-10"><a href="#cite_note-anselme-1">[1]</a></sup> He was to prove a weak ruler; his reign was effectively a series of distinct regimes, depending who held the effective reins of power. At first, Marie de Medici, his mother, served as regent and advanced a pro-Spanish policy. To deal with the financial troubles of France, Louis summoned the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_States-General" title="French States-General">Estates General</a> in 1614; this would be the last time that body met until the eve of the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>. Marie arranged the 1615 marriage of Louis to <a href="/wiki/Anne_of_Austria" title="Anne of Austria">Anne of Austria</a>, the daughter of King <a href="/wiki/Philip_III_of_Spain" title="Philip III of Spain">Philip III of Spain</a>.</p>
<p>In 1617, however, Louis conspired with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_de_Luynes" title="Charles de Luynes">Charles d'Albert, duc de Luynes</a> to dispense with her influence, having her favorite <a href="/wiki/Concino_Concini" title="Concino Concini">Concino Concini</a> assassinated on 26 April of that year. After some years of weak government by Louis's favorites, the King made <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armand_Jean_du_Plessis,_Cardinal_Richelieu" title="Armand Jean du Plessis, Cardinal Richelieu">Armand Jean du Plessis, Cardinal Richelieu</a>, a former protégé of his mother, the chief minister of France in 1624.</p>
<p>Richelieu advanced an anti-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habsburg" title="Habsburg">Habsburg</a> policy. He arranged for Louis' sister, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henrietta_Maria" title="Henrietta Maria">Henrietta Maria</a>, to marry King <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_England" title="Charles I of England">Charles I of England</a>, on 11 May 1625. Her pro-Catholic propaganda in England was one of the contributing factors to the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">English Civil War</a>. Richelieu, as ambitious for France and the French monarchy as for himself, laid the ground for the <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolute monarchy</a> that would last in France until the Revolution. He wanted to establish a dominating position for France in Europe, and he wanted to unify France under the monarchy. He established the role of <i><a href="/wiki/Intendant" title="Intendant">intendants</a></i>, non-noble men whose arbitrary powers of administration were granted (and revocable) by the monarch, superseding many of the traditional duties and privileges of the noble governors.</p>
<p>Although it required a succession of internal military campaigns, he disarmed the fortified Huguenot towns that Henry had allowed. He involved France in the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a> (1618–1648) against the Habsburgs by <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_B%C3%A4rwalde" title="Treaty of Bärwalde">concluding an alliance with Sweden</a> in 1631 and, actively, in 1635. He died in 1642 before the conclusion of that conflict, having groomed Cardinal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jules_Mazarin" title="Jules Mazarin">Jules Mazarin</a> as a successor. Louis XIII outlived him but by one year, dying in 1643 at the age of forty-two. After a childless marriage for twenty-three years his queen, Anne, delivered a son on 5 September 1638, whom he named Louis after himself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anselme_1-11"><a href="#cite_note-anselme-1">[1]</a></sup> In the mid eighteenth century, the Bourbon monarchy had a faulty system for finance and taxation. Their lacking a national bank lead to them taking short-term loans, and ordering financial agents to make payments in advance or in excess of tax revenues collected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Louis_XIV_and_Louis_XV">Louis XIV and Louis XV</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Bourbon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Louis XIV and Louis XV">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grand_Royal_Coat_of_Arms_of_France_%26_Navarre.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1542" data-file-width="1190" height="259" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Grand_Royal_Coat_of_Arms_of_France_%26_Navarre.svg/200px-Grand_Royal_Coat_of_Arms_of_France_%26_Navarre.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Grand_Royal_Coat_of_Arms_of_France_%26_Navarre.svg/300px-Grand_Royal_Coat_of_Arms_of_France_%26_Navarre.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Grand_Royal_Coat_of_Arms_of_France_%26_Navarre.svg/400px-Grand_Royal_Coat_of_Arms_of_France_%26_Navarre.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Grand_Royal_Coat_of_Arms_of_France_%26_Navarre.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Royal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emblem_of_France" title="Emblem of France">Coat of Arms of the Kingdom of France and Navarre</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV_of_France" title="Louis XIV of France">Louis XIV of France</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Louis_XV_of_France" title="Louis XV of France">Louis XV of France</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV_of_France" title="Louis XIV of France">Louis XIV</a> succeeded his father at four years of age;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anselme_1-12"><a href="#cite_note-anselme-1">[1]</a></sup> he would go on to become the most powerful king in French history. His mother Anne served as his regent with her favorite Jules, Cardinal Mazarin, as chief minister. Mazarin continued the policies of Richelieu, bringing the Thirty Years' War to a successful conclusion in 1648 and defeating the nobility's challenge to royal absolutism in a series of civil wars known as the <a href="/wiki/Fronde" title="Fronde">Frondes</a>. He continued to war with Spain until 1659.</p>
<p>In that year the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_the_Pyrenees" title="Treaty of the Pyrenees">Treaty of the Pyrenees</a> was signed signifying a major shift in power, France had replaced Spain as the dominant state in Europe. The treaty called for an <a href="/wiki/Arranged_marriage" title="Arranged marriage">arranged marriage</a> between Louis and his cousin <a href="/wiki/Maria_Theresa_of_Spain" title="Maria Theresa of Spain">Maria Theresa</a>, a daughter of King <a href="/wiki/Philip_IV_of_Spain" title="Philip IV of Spain">Philip IV of Spain</a> by his first wife Elisabeth, the sister of Louis XIII. They were married in 1660 and had a son, Louis, in 1661.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anselme_1-13"><a href="#cite_note-anselme-1">[1]</a></sup> Mazarin died on 9 March 1661 and it was expected that Louis would appoint another chief minister, as had become the tradition, but instead he shocked the country by announcing he would rule alone.</p>
<p>For six years Louis reformed the finances of his state and built formidable armed forces. France fought a series of wars from 1667 onward and gained some territory on its northern and eastern borders. Maria Theresa died in 1683 and the next year he secretly married the devoutly Catholic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7oise_d%27Aubign%C3%A9,_marquise_de_Maintenon" title="Françoise d'Aubigné, marquise de Maintenon">Françoise d'Aubigné, marquise de Maintenon</a>. Louis XIV began to persecute Protestants, undoing the religious tolerance established by his grandfather Henry IV, culminating in his revocation of the Edict of Nantes in 1685.</p>
<p>The last war waged by Louis XIV proved to be one of the most important to dynastic Europe. In 1700, King <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_Spain" title="Charles II of Spain">Charles II of Spain</a>, a Habsburg, died without a son. Louis's son the <i>Grand Dauphin</i>, as the late king's nephew, was the closest heir, and Charles willed the kingdom to the Dauphin's second son, the Duke of Anjou. Other powers, particularly the Austrian Habsburgs, who had the next closest claims, objected to such a vast increase in French power.</p>
<p>Initially, most of the other powers were willing to accept Anjou's reign as <a href="/wiki/Philip_V_of_Spain" title="Philip V of Spain">Philip V</a>, but Louis's mishandling of their concerns soon drove the English, Dutch and other powers to join the Austrians in a coalition against France. The <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a> began in 1701 and raged for 12 years. In the end Louis's grandson was recognized as king of Spain, but he was obliged to agree to the forfeiture of succession rights in France, the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Spain" title="Habsburg Spain">Spanish Habsburgs</a>' other European territories were largely ceded to Austria, and France was nearly bankrupted by the cost of the struggle. Louis died on 1 September 1715 ending his seventy-two year reign, the longest in European history.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:362px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Louis_XIV_of_France_and_his_family_attributed_to_Nicolas_de_Largilli%C3%A8re.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1007" data-file-width="1280" height="283" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Louis_XIV_of_France_and_his_family_attributed_to_Nicolas_de_Largilli%C3%A8re.jpg/360px-Louis_XIV_of_France_and_his_family_attributed_to_Nicolas_de_Largilli%C3%A8re.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Louis_XIV_of_France_and_his_family_attributed_to_Nicolas_de_Largilli%C3%A8re.jpg/540px-Louis_XIV_of_France_and_his_family_attributed_to_Nicolas_de_Largilli%C3%A8re.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Louis_XIV_of_France_and_his_family_attributed_to_Nicolas_de_Largilli%C3%A8re.jpg/720px-Louis_XIV_of_France_and_his_family_attributed_to_Nicolas_de_Largilli%C3%A8re.jpg 2x" width="360"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Louis_XIV_of_France_and_his_family_attributed_to_Nicolas_de_Largilli%C3%A8re.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dynastic group portrait of Louis XIV (seated) with his son <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis,_Dauphin_of_France_(1661%E2%80%931711)" title="Louis, Dauphin of France (1661–1711)">le Grand Dauphin</a></i> (to the left), his grandson <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis_of_France,_Duke_of_Burgundy" title="Louis of France, Duke of Burgundy">Louis, Duke of Burgundy</a> (to the right), his great-grandson the duc d'Anjou, later Louis XV, and <a href="/wiki/Madame_de_Ventadour" title="Madame de Ventadour">Madame de Ventadour</a>, his governess, who commissioned this painting some years later; busts of <a href="/wiki/Henry_IV_of_France" title="Henry IV of France">Henry IV</a> and <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIII_of_France" title="Louis XIII of France">Louis XIII</a> in the background.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The reign of Louis XIV was so long that he outlived both his son and eldest grandson. He was succeeded by his great-grandson <a href="/wiki/Louis_XV_of_France" title="Louis XV of France">Louis XV</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anselme_1-14"><a href="#cite_note-anselme-1">[1]</a></sup> Louis XV was born on 15 February 1710 and was thus aged only five at his ascension, the third Louis in a row to become king of France before the age of ten. Initially, the regency was held by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philip_II,_Duke_of_Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Philip II, Duke of Orléans">Philip, Duke of Orléans</a>, Louis XIV's nephew, as nearest adult male to the throne.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anselme_1-15"><a href="#cite_note-anselme-1">[1]</a></sup> This <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regence" title="Regence">Regence</a></i> was seen as a period of greater individual expression, manifested in secular, artistic, literary and colonial activity, in contrast to the austere latter years of Louis XIV's reign.</p>
<p>Following Orléans' death in 1723, the <a href="/wiki/Louis_Henri,_Duke_of_Bourbon" title="Louis Henri, Duke of Bourbon">Duke of Bourbon</a>, representative of the Bourbon-Condé cadet line, became prime minister. It was expected that Louis would marry his cousin, the daughter of King Philip V of Spain, but this engagement was broken by the duke in 1725 so that Louis could marry <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maria_Leszczynska" title="Maria Leszczynska">Maria Leszczynska</a>, the daughter of Stanislas, former king of Poland. Bourbon's motive appears to have been a desire to produce an heir as soon as possible so as to reduce the chances of a succession dispute between Philip V and the Duke of Orléans in the event of the sickly king's death. Maria was already an adult woman at the time of the marriage, while the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infanta" title="Infanta">infanta</a> was still a young girl.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:362px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Louis14-Family.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1081" data-file-width="1500" height="259" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Louis14-Family.jpg/360px-Louis14-Family.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Louis14-Family.jpg/540px-Louis14-Family.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Louis14-Family.jpg/720px-Louis14-Family.jpg 2x" width="360"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Louis14-Family.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A posthumous painting commissioned around 1670 by <a href="/wiki/Philippe_I,_Duke_of_Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Philippe I, Duke of Orléans">Philippe de France</a>. It shows the French Bourbon Family around that time. It includes: <a href="/wiki/Henrietta_Maria_of_France" title="Henrietta Maria of France">Henrietta Maria of France</a> (died 1669), exiled Queen of England; <a href="/wiki/Philippe_I,_Duke_of_Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Philippe I, Duke of Orléans">Philippe I, Duke of Orléans</a>, founder of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Orl%C3%A9ans" title="House of Orléans">House of Orléans</a>; his first wife <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henrietta_Anne_Stuart" title="Henrietta Anne Stuart">Princess Henriette</a> (died 1670); the couple's first daughter <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marie_Louise_d%27Orl%C3%A9ans_(1662%E2%80%931689)" title="Marie Louise d'Orléans (1662–1689)">Marie Louise d'Orléans</a> (later Queen of Spain); <a href="/wiki/Anne_of_Austria" title="Anne of Austria">Anne of Austria</a> (died 1666); the Orléans daughters of <a href="/wiki/Gaston,_Duke_of_Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Gaston, Duke of Orléans">Gaston de France</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis_XIV" title="Louis XIV">Louis XIV</a>; the Dauphin of France with his wife <a href="/wiki/Maria_Theresa_of_Spain" title="Maria Theresa of Spain">Maria Theresa of Spain</a> with her third daughter <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Princess_Marie-Th%C3%A9r%C3%A8se_of_France_(1667%E2%80%931672)" title="Princess Marie-Thérèse of France (1667–1672)">Marie-Thérèse de France</a>, called <a href="/wiki/Madame_Royale" title="Madame Royale">Madame Royale</a> (died 1672) and her second son <i>Philippe-Charles de France, duc d'Anjou</i> (d1671). The first daughter of Gaston stands on the far right: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anne,_Duchess_of_Montpensier" title="Anne, Duchess of Montpensier">Anne Marie Louise d'Orléans</a>. The picture frame with the 2 children are the other 2 daughters of Louis and Maria Theresa who died in 1662 and 1664.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Nevertheless, Bourbon's action brought a very negative response from Spain, and for his incompetence Bourbon was soon replaced by Cardinal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andre_Hercule_de_Fleury" title="Andre Hercule de Fleury">Andre Hercule de Fleury</a>, the young king's tutor, in 1726. Fleury was a peace-loving man who intended to keep France out of war, but circumstances presented themselves that made this impossible.</p>
<p>The first cause of these wars came in 1733 when <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Augustus_II_of_Poland" title="Augustus II of Poland">Augustus II</a>, the elector of Saxony and king of Poland died. With French support, Stanislas was again elected king. This brought France into conflict with Russia and Austria who supported <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Augustus_III" title="Augustus III">Augustus III</a>, Elector of Saxony and son of Augustus II.</p>
<p>Stanislas lost the Polish crown, but he was given the Duchy of Lorraine as compensation, which would pass to France after his death. Next came the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Austrian_Succession" title="War of the Austrian Succession">War of the Austrian Succession</a> in 1740 in which France supported King <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frederick_II_of_Prussia" title="Frederick II of Prussia">Frederick II of Prussia</a> against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maria_Theresa_of_Austria" title="Maria Theresa of Austria">Maria Theresa</a>, Archduchess of Austria and Queen of Hungary. Fleury died in 1743 before the conclusion of the war.</p>
<p>Shortly after Fleury's death in 1745 Louis was influenced by his mistress the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marquise_de_Pompadour" title="Marquise de Pompadour">Marquise de Pompadour</a> to reverse the policy of France in 1756 by creating an alliance with Austria against Prussia in the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a>. The war was a disaster for France, which lost most of her overseas possessions to the British in the Treaty of Paris in 1763. Maria, his wife, died in 1768 and Louis himself died on 10 May 1774.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_Revolution">French Revolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Bourbon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: French Revolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Louis_XVI_of_France" title="Louis XVI of France">Louis XVI</a> had become the <a href="/wiki/Dauphin_of_France" title="Dauphin of France">Dauphin of France</a> upon the death of his father <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis,_Dauphin_of_France_(1729%E2%80%931765)" title="Louis, Dauphin of France (1729–1765)">Louis</a>, the son of Louis XV, in 1765. He married <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marie_Antoinette_of_Austria" title="Marie Antoinette of Austria">Marie Antoinette of Austria</a>, a daughter of Holy Roman Empress Maria Theresa, in 1770. Louis intervened in the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a> against Britain in 1778, but he is most remembered for his role in the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>. France was in financial turmoil and Louis was forced to convene the <a href="/wiki/Estates-General_of_1789" title="Estates-General of 1789">Estates-General</a> on 5 May 1789.</p>
<p>They formed the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(French_Revolution)" title="National Assembly (French Revolution)">National Assembly</a> and forced Louis to accept a constitution that limited his powers on 14 July 1790. He <a href="/wiki/Flight_to_Varennes" title="Flight to Varennes">tried to flee France</a> in June 1791, but was captured. The French monarchy was abolished on 21 September 1792 and <a href="/wiki/French_First_Republic" title="French First Republic">a republic</a> was proclaimed. The chain of Bourbon monarchs begun in 1589 was broken. Louis XVI was executed on 21 January 1793.</p>
<p>Marie Antoinette and her son, Louis, were held as prisoners. Many French royalists proclaimed him <a href="/wiki/Louis_XVII_of_France" title="Louis XVII of France">Louis XVII</a>, but he never reigned. She was executed on 16 October 1793. He died of <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> on 8 June 1795 at the age of ten while in captivity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/French_Revolutionary_Wars" title="French Revolutionary Wars">French Revolutionary Wars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a> spread nationalism and anti-absolutism throughout Europe, and the other Bourbon monarchs were threatened. <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_I_of_the_Two_Sicilies" title="Ferdinand I of the Two Sicilies">Ferdinand</a> was forced to flee from Naples in 1806 when <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napoleon_Bonaparte" title="Napoleon Bonaparte">Napoleon Bonaparte</a> deposed him and installed his brother, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Bonaparte" title="Joseph Bonaparte">Joseph</a>, as king. Ferdinand continued to rule from Sicily until 1815.</p>
<p>Napoleon conquered Parma in 1800 and compensated the Bourbon duke with <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Etruria" title="Kingdom of Etruria">Etruria</a>, a new kingdom he created from the Grand Duchy of Tuscany. It was short-lived, counting only two monarchs, <a href="/wiki/Louis_I_of_Etruria" title="Louis I of Etruria">Louis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_II,_Duke_of_Parma" title="Charles II, Duke of Parma">Charles</a>, as Napoleon annexed Etruria in 1807.</p>
<p>King <a href="/wiki/Charles_IV_of_Spain" title="Charles IV of Spain">Charles IV of Spain</a> had been an ally of France. He succeeded his father, <a href="/wiki/Charles_III_of_Spain" title="Charles III of Spain">Charles III</a>, in 1788. At first he declared war on France on 7 March 1793, but he made peace on 22 June 1795. This peace became an alliance on 19 August 1796. His chief minister, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manuel_de_Godoy" title="Manuel de Godoy">Manuel de Godoy</a> convinced Charles that his son, Ferdinand, was plotting to overthrow him. Napoleon exploited the situation and invaded Spain in March 1808. This led to an uprising that forced Charles to abdicate on 19 March in favor of his son, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ferdinand_VII" title="Ferdinand VII">Ferdinand VII</a>. Napoleon forced Ferdinand to return the crown to Charles on 30 April and then convinced Charles to relinquish it to him on 10 May. In turn, he gave it to his brother, Joseph, king of Naples on 6 June. Joseph abandoned Naples to <a href="/wiki/Joachim_Murat" title="Joachim Murat">Joachim Murat</a>, the husband of Napoleon's sister. This was very unpopular in Spain and resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">Peninsular War</a>, a struggle that would contribute to the downfall of Napoleon.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bourbon_Restoration">Bourbon Restoration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Bourbon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Bourbon Restoration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pavillon_royal_de_France.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1500" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Pavillon_royal_de_France.svg/250px-Pavillon_royal_de_France.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Pavillon_royal_de_France.svg/375px-Pavillon_royal_de_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Pavillon_royal_de_France.svg/500px-Pavillon_royal_de_France.svg.png 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pavillon_royal_de_France.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The standard of the French royal family under the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Early_Modern_France" title="Early Modern France">Ancien Régime</a></i> and the <a href="/wiki/Bourbon_Restoration" title="Bourbon Restoration">restoration period</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bourbon_Restoration" title="Bourbon Restoration">Bourbon Restoration</a></div>
<p>With the abdication of Napoleon on 11 April 1814 the Bourbon dynasty was restored to the kingdom of France in the person of <a href="/wiki/Louis_XVIII_of_France" title="Louis XVIII of France">Louis XVIII</a>, brother of Louis XVI. Napoleon escaped from exile and Louis fled in March 1815. Louis was again restored after the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Waterloo" title="Battle of Waterloo">Battle of Waterloo</a> on 7 July.</p>
<p>The conservative elements of Europe dominated the post-Napoleonic age, but the values of the French Revolution could not be easily swept aside. Louis granted a constitution on 14 June 1814 to appease the liberals, but the ultra-royalist party, led by his brother, Charles, continued to influence his reign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Durant_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Durant-5">[5]</a></sup> When he died in 1824 his brother became king as <a href="/wiki/Charles_X_of_France" title="Charles X of France">Charles X</a> much to the dismay of French liberals. In a saying ascribed to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Talleyrand" title="Talleyrand">Talleyrand</a>, "they had learned nothing and forgotten nothing".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Bourbon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Charles passed several laws that appealed to the upper class, but angered the middle class. The situation came to a head when he appointed a new minister on 8 August 1829 who did not have the confidence of the chamber. The chamber censured the king on 18 March 1830 and in response Charles proclaimed five ordinances on 26 July intended to silence criticism against him.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> This almost resulted in another revolution as dramatic as the one in 1789, but moderates were able to control the situation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_the_July_Monarchy_(1830-31).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1339" data-file-width="1092" height="270" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Coat_of_Arms_of_the_July_Monarchy_%281830-31%29.svg/220px-Coat_of_Arms_of_the_July_Monarchy_%281830-31%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Coat_of_Arms_of_the_July_Monarchy_%281830-31%29.svg/330px-Coat_of_Arms_of_the_July_Monarchy_%281830-31%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Coat_of_Arms_of_the_July_Monarchy_%281830-31%29.svg/440px-Coat_of_Arms_of_the_July_Monarchy_%281830-31%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_the_July_Monarchy_(1830-31).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Coat of Arms of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis-Philippe_of_France" title="Louis-Philippe of France">Louis-Philippe</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orleanist" title="Orleanist">Orleanist</a> cadet branch, French king during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/July_monarchy" title="July monarchy">July monarchy</a> 1830-48 (with the revolutionary <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_France" title="Flag of France">Tricolour flag</a> and the Napoleonic Order of the <a href="/wiki/Legion_of_Honour" title="Legion of Honour">Legion of Honour</a>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As a compromise the crown was offered to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis-Philippe_of_France" title="Louis-Philippe of France">Louis-Philippe</a>, duke of Orléans, a descendant of <a href="/wiki/Philippe_I,_Duke_of_Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Philippe I, Duke of Orléans">the brother of Louis XIV</a>, and the head of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orleanist" title="Orleanist">Orleanist</a> cadet branch of the Bourbons. Agreeing to reign constitutionally and under the <a href="/wiki/Tricolour_(flag)" title="Tricolour (flag)">tricolour</a>, he was proclaimed King of the French on 7 August. The resulting regime, known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/July_monarchy" title="July monarchy">July monarchy</a>, lasted until the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolution_of_1848_in_France" title="Revolution of 1848 in France">Revolution of 1848</a>. The Bourbon monarchy in France ended on 24 February 1848, when Louis-Philippe was forced to abdicate and the short-lived <a href="/wiki/French_Second_Republic" title="French Second Republic">Second Republic</a> was established.</p>
<p>Some <a href="/wiki/Legitimists" title="Legitimists">legitimists</a> refused to recognize the Orleanist monarchy. After the death of Charles in 1836 his son was proclaimed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis-Antoine,_Duke_of_Angoul%C3%AAme" title="Louis-Antoine, Duke of Angoulême">Louis XIX</a>, though this title was never formally recognized. Charles' grandson <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henri,_comte_de_Chambord" title="Henri, comte de Chambord">Henri, comte de Chambord</a>, the last Bourbon claimant of the French crown, was proclaimed by some Henry V, but the French monarchy was never restored.</p>
<p>Following the 1870 collapse of the empire of Emperor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napoleon_III_of_France" title="Napoleon III of France">Napoleon III</a>, Henri was offered a restored throne. However Chambord refused to accept the throne unless France abandoned the revolution-inspired <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_France" title="Flag of France">tricolour</a> and accepted what he regarded as the true Bourbon flag of France, featuring the <a href="/wiki/Fleur-de-lis" title="Fleur-de-lis">fleur-de-lis</a>. The tricolour, originally associated with the French Revolution and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_French_Republic" title="First French Republic">First Republic</a>, had been used by the July Monarchy, the Second Republic and both Empires; the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_National_Assembly" title="French National Assembly">French National Assembly</a> could not possibly agree.</p>
<p>A <i>temporary</i> <a href="/wiki/French_Third_Republic" title="French Third Republic">Third Republic</a> was established, while monarchists waited for the comte de Chambord to die and for the succession to pass to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis-Philippe,_Comte_de_Paris" title="Louis-Philippe, Comte de Paris">Comte de Paris</a>, who was willing to accept the tricolour. Henri lived until 1883, by which time public opinion had come to accept the republic as the "form of government that divides us least." His death without issue marked the extinction of the French Bourbons. Thus the head of the House of Bourbon became <a href="/wiki/Juan,_Count_of_Montiz%C3%B3n" title="Juan, Count of Montizón">Juan, Count of Montizón</a> of the Spanish line of the house who was also <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carlist" title="Carlist">Carlist</a> claimant to the throne of Spain, and had become the senior male of the dynasty by primogeniture. His heir as eldest Bourbon and head of the house is today <a href="/wiki/Louis_Alphonse,_Duke_of_Anjou" title="Louis Alphonse, Duke of Anjou">Louis Alphonse, Duke of Anjou</a>.</p>
<p>By an ordinance of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis_Philippe_I_of_France" title="Louis Philippe I of France">Louis Philippe I of France</a> of 13 August 1830, it was decided that the king's children (and his sister) would continue to bear the arms of Orléans, that Louis-Philippe's eldest son, as Prince Royal, would bear the title of duc d'Orléans, that the younger sons would continue to have their existing titles, and that the sister and daughters of the king would be styled <i>Royal Highness</i> and "d'Orléans", but the Orléans dynasts did not take the name "of France".</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Bourbons_of_Spain_and_Italy">Bourbons of Spain and Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Bourbon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Bourbons of Spain and Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philip_V">Philip V</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Bourbon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Philip V">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_Spanish_Monarch.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="949" data-file-width="630" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Coat_of_Arms_of_Spanish_Monarch.svg/150px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Spanish_Monarch.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Coat_of_Arms_of_Spanish_Monarch.svg/225px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Spanish_Monarch.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Coat_of_Arms_of_Spanish_Monarch.svg/300px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Spanish_Monarch.svg.png 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_Spanish_Monarch.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Arms of the present King of Spain of the House of Bourbon</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Spanish branch of the House of Bourbon was founded by Philip V. He was born in 1683 in Versailles, the second son of the Grand Dauphin, son of Louis XIV. He was Duke of <a href="/wiki/Anjou" title="Anjou">Anjou</a> and probably never expected to be raised to a rank higher than that. However King <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_Spain" title="Charles II of Spain">Charles II of Spain</a>, dying without issue, willed the throne to his grand-nephew the Duke of Anjou, younger grandson of his eldest sister <a href="/wiki/Maria_Theresa_of_Spain" title="Maria Theresa of Spain">Marie-Thérèse</a>, daughter of King <a href="/wiki/Philip_IV_of_Spain" title="Philip IV of Spain">Philip IV of Spain</a> who had married Louis XIV of France.</p>
<p>The prospect of Bourbons on both the French and Spanish thrones was resisted as creating an <a href="/wiki/European_balance_of_power" title="European balance of power">imbalance of power</a> in Europe by its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Historical_powers" title="Historical powers">dominant regimes</a> and, upon Charles II's death on 1 November 1700, a <a href="/wiki/Grand_Alliance_(League_of_Augsburg)" title="Grand Alliance (League of Augsburg)">Grand Alliance</a> of European nations united against Philip. This was known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_of_Spanish_Succession" title="War of Spanish Succession">War of Spanish Succession</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Utrecht" title="Treaty of Utrecht">Treaty of Utrecht</a>, signed on 11 April 1713, Philip was recognized as king of Spain but his renunciation of succession rights to France was affirmed and, of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>'s other European territories, Sicily was ceded to Savoy, and the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Netherlands" title="Spanish Netherlands">Spanish Netherlands</a>, Milan and Naples were allotted to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">Austrian Habsburgs</a>.</p>
<p>Philip had two sons by his first wife. After her death he married <a href="/wiki/Elisabeth_Farnese" title="Elisabeth Farnese">Elisabeth Farnese</a>, niece of <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Farnese,_Duke_of_Parma" title="Francesco Farnese, Duke of Parma">Francesco Farnese, Duke of Parma</a>, in 1714. She presented Philip with three sons, for whom she had ambitions of securing Italian crowns. Thus she induced Philip to occupy Sardinia and Sicily in 1717.</p>
<p>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quadruple_Alliance_(1718)" title="Quadruple Alliance (1718)">Quadruple Alliance</a> of Britain, France, Austria and the Netherlands was organized on 2 August 1718 to stop him. In the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_The_Hague_(1720)" title="Treaty of The Hague (1720)">Treaty of The Hague</a>, signed on 17 February 1720, Philip renounced his conquests of Sardinia and Sicily, but assured the ascension of his eldest son by Elisabeth to the Duchy of Parma upon the reigning duke's death. Philip abdicated in January 1724 in favor of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis_of_Spain" title="Louis of Spain">Louis I</a>, his eldest son with his first wife, but Louis died in August and Philip resumed the crown.</p>
<p>When the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Polish_Succession" title="War of the Polish Succession">War of the Polish Succession</a> began in 1733, Philip and Elisabeth saw another opportunity to advance the claims of their sons and recover at least part of the former possessions of the Spanish crown on the Italian peninsula. Philip signed the <a href="/wiki/Pacte_de_Famille" title="Pacte de Famille">Family Compact</a> with Louis XV, his nephew and king of France. Charles, Duke of Parma since 1731, invaded Naples. At the conclusion of peace on 13 November 1738, control of Parma and Piacenza was ceded to Austria, which had occupied the duchies but was now forced to recognise Charles as King of Naples and Sicily. Philip also used the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Austrian_Succession" title="War of the Austrian Succession">War of the Austrian Succession</a> to win more territory in Italy. He did not live to see it to its conclusion, however, dying in 1746.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ferdinand_VI_and_Charles_III">Ferdinand VI and Charles III</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Bourbon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Ferdinand VI and Charles III">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ferdinand_VI" title="Ferdinand VI">Ferdinand VI</a>, second son of Philip V and his first wife, succeeded his father. He was a peace-loving monarch who kept Spain out of the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a>. He died in 1759 in the midst of that conflict and was succeeded by his half-brother <a href="/wiki/Charles_III_of_Spain" title="Charles III of Spain">Charles III</a>. Charles was the eldest son of Philip and Elisabeth Farnese. He was born in 1716 and had become Duke of Parma when the last Farnese duke died in 1731.</p>
<p>Following Spain's victory over the Austrians at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bitonto" title="Battle of Bitonto">battle of Bitonto</a>, it proved inexpedient to reunite Naples and Sicily to Spain, so as a compromise Charles became King of Naples, as Charles IV and VII of Sicily. Following Charles' accession to the Spanish throne in 1759 he was required, by the Treaty of Naples of 3 October 1759, to abdicate Naples and Sicily to his third son, <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_I_of_the_Two_Sicilies" title="Ferdinand I of the Two Sicilies">Ferdinand</a>, thus initiating the branch known as the Neapolitan Bourbons.</p>
<p>Charles revived the Family Compact with France on 15 August 1761 and joined in the Seven Years' War against Britain in 1762; the reformist policies he had espoused in Naples were pursued with similar energy in Spain, where he completely overhauled the cumbersome bureaucracy of the state. As a French ally he opposed Britain during the American Revolution in June 1779, supplying large quantities of weapons and munitions to the rebels and keeping one third of all the British forces in the Americas occupied defending Florida and what is now <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">Alabama</a>, which were ultimately recaptured by Spain. Charles died in 1788.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bourbons_of_Parma">Bourbons of Parma</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Bourbon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Bourbons of Parma">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Elisabeth Farnese's ambitions were realized at the conclusion of the War of the Austrian Succession in 1748 when the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Parma_and_Piacenza" title="Duchy of Parma and Piacenza">Duchy of Parma and Piacenza</a>, already occupied by Spanish troops, were ceded by Austria to her second son, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philip_of_Parma" title="Philip of Parma">Philip</a>, and combined with the former <a href="/wiki/House_of_Gonzaga" title="House of Gonzaga">Gonzaga</a> duchy of <a href="/wiki/Guastalla" title="Guastalla">Guastalla</a>. Elisabeth died in 1766.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_Bourbon_monarchs_outside_France">Later Bourbon monarchs outside France</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Bourbon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Later Bourbon monarchs outside France">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<div class="thumb tright">

<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ducal_Coat_of_Arms_of_Parma_(1748-1802).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Coat of Arms of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bourbon-Parma" title="House of Bourbon-Parma">House of Bourbon Spain-Parma</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Upon the fall of the French Empire, Ferdinand I was restored to the throne of the Kingdom of the Two Sicilies in 1815, founding the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bourbon-Two_Sicilies" title="House of Bourbon-Two Sicilies">House of Bourbon-Two Sicilies</a>. His subjects revolted in 1820 and he was forced to grant a constitution; Austria invaded in March 1821 and revoked the constitution. He was succeeded by his son, <a href="/wiki/Francis_I_of_the_Two_Sicilies" title="Francis I of the Two Sicilies">Francis I</a>, in 1825 and by his grandson, <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_II_of_the_Two_Sicilies" title="Ferdinand II of the Two Sicilies">Ferdinand II</a>, in 1830. Another revolution erupted in January 1848 and Ferdinand was also forced to grant a constitution. This constitution was revoked in 1849. Ferdinand was succeeded by his son, <a href="/wiki/Francis_II_of_the_Two_Sicilies" title="Francis II of the Two Sicilies">Francis II</a>, in May 1859.</p>
<p>When <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Garibaldi" title="Giuseppe Garibaldi">Giuseppe Garibaldi</a> captured Naples in 1860, Francis restored the constitution in an attempt to save his sovereignty. He fled to the fortress of <a href="/wiki/Gaeta" title="Gaeta">Gaeta</a>, which was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siege_of_Gaeta_(1861)" title="Siege of Gaeta (1861)">captured by the Piedmontese troops</a> in February 1861; his kingdom was incorporated into the Kingdom of Italy on 17 March 1861, after the fall the fortress of <a href="/wiki/Messina" title="Messina">Messina</a> (surrendered on 12 March), although the Neapolitan troops in <a href="/wiki/Civitella_del_Tronto" title="Civitella del Tronto">Civitella del Tronto</a> resisted three days longer.</p>
<p>After the fall of Napoleon, Napoleon's wife, <a href="/wiki/Marie_Louise,_Duchess_of_Parma" title="Marie Louise, Duchess of Parma">Maria Louisa</a>, was made Duchess of Parma. As compensation, Charles Louis, the former king of Etruria, was made the Duke of Lucca. When Maria Louisa died in 1847 he was restored to Parma as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_Parma" title="Charles II of Parma">Charles II</a>. Lucca was incorporated into Tuscany. He was succeeded by his son, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_III_of_Parma" title="Charles III of Parma">Charles III</a>, and grandson, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_I_of_Parma" title="Robert I of Parma">Robert I</a>, in 1854. The people of Parma voted for a union with the kingdom of Sardinia in 1860. After Italian unification the next year, the Bourbon dynasty in Italy was no more.</p>
<p>Ferdinand VII was restored to the throne of Spain in March 1814. Like his Italian Bourbon counterpart, his subjects revolted against him in January 1820 and he was forced to grant a constitution. A French army invaded in 1823 and the constitution was revoked. Ferdinand married his fourth wife, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maria_Christina_of_Bourbon-Two_Sicilies" title="Maria Christina of Bourbon-Two Sicilies">Maria Christina</a>, the daughter of Francis I, the Bourbon king of Sicily, in 1829. Despite his many marriages he did not have a son, so in 1833 he was influenced by his wife to abolish the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salic_Law" title="Salic Law">Salic Law</a> so that her daughter, Isabella, could become queen depriving his brother, <a href="/wiki/Infante_Carlos,_Count_of_Molina" title="Infante Carlos, Count of Molina">Don Carlos</a>, of the throne.</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isabella_II_of_Spain" title="Isabella II of Spain">Isabella II</a> succeeded her father when he died in 1833. She was only three years old and Maria Cristina, her mother, served as regent. Maria knew that she needed the support of the liberals to oppose Don Carlos so she granted a constitution in 1834. Don Carlos found his <a href="/wiki/Carlism" title="Carlism">greatest support</a> in Catalonia and the Basques country because the constitution centralized the provinces thus denying them the autonomy they sought. He was defeated and fled the country in 1839. Isabella was declared of age in 1843 and she married her cousin Francisco de Asis, the son of her father's brother, on 10 October 1846. A military revolution broke out against Isabella in 1868 and she was deposed on 29 September. She abdicated in favor of her son, Alfonso, in 1870, but Spain was proclaimed a republic for a brief time.</p>
<p>When the <a href="/wiki/First_Spanish_Republic" title="First Spanish Republic">First Spanish Republic</a> failed the crown was offered to Isabella's son who accepted on 1 January 1875 as <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_XII_of_Spain" title="Alfonso XII of Spain">Alfonso XII</a>. <a href="/wiki/Carlos,_Duke_of_Madrid" title="Carlos, Duke of Madrid">Don Carlos</a>, who returned to Spain, was again defeated and resumed his exile in February 1876. Alfonso granted a new constitution in July 1876 that was more liberal than the one granted by his grandmother. His reign was cut short when he died in 1885 at the age of twenty-eight.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Alfonso_XIII_of_Spain" title="Alfonso XIII of Spain">Alfonso XIII</a> was born on 17 May 1886 after the death of his father. His mother, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Christina_of_Austria" title="Maria Christina of Austria">Maria Christina</a>, the second wife of Alfonso XII served as regent. Alfonso XIII was declared of age in 1902 and he married Victoria Eugénie Julia Ena of Battenberg, the granddaughter of the British queen <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Victoria_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Victoria of the United Kingdom">Victoria</a>, on 31 May 1906. He remained neutral during World War I, but supported the military coup of <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Primo_de_Rivera" title="Miguel Primo de Rivera">Miguel Primo de Rivera</a> on 13 September 1923. A movement towards the establishment of a republic began in 1930 and Alfonso fled the country on 14 April 1931. He never formally abdicated, but lived the rest of his life in exile. He died in 1941.</p>
<p>The Bourbon dynasty seemed finished in Spain as in the rest of the world, but it would be resurrected. The Second Spanish Republic was overthrown in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>, leading to the dictatorship of <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a>. He named <a href="/wiki/Juan_Carlos_I_of_Spain" title="Juan Carlos I of Spain">Juan Carlos de Borbón</a>, a grandson of Alfonso XIII, his successor in 1969. When Franco died six years later, Juan Carlos I took the throne to restore the Bourbon dynasty. The new king oversaw the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_transition_to_democracy" title="Spanish transition to democracy">Spanish transition to democracy</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution_of_1978" title="Spanish Constitution of 1978">Spanish Constitution of 1978</a> recognized the monarchy.</p>
<p>Since 1964 the Bourbon-Parma line has reigned agnatically in Luxembourg through Grand Dukes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jean_of_Luxembourg" title="Jean of Luxembourg">Jean</a> and his son <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henri_of_Luxembourg" title="Henri of Luxembourg">Henri</a>. In June 2011, Luxembourg adopted absolute primogeniture, replacing the old Semi-Salic law that might have guaranteed the survival of Bourbon rule for generations.</p>
<p>Though it is not as powerful as it once was and no longer reigns in its native country of France, the House of Bourbon is by no means extinct and has survived to the present-day world, predominantly composed of republics.</p>
<p>The House of Bourbon, in its surviving branches, is believed to be the oldest royal dynasty of Europe (and the oldest documented European family altogether) that is still existing in the direct male line today: The <a href="/wiki/House_of_Capet" title="House of Capet">House of Capet</a>'s male ancestors, the <a href="/wiki/Robertians" title="Robertians">Robertians</a>, go back to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_of_Hesbaye" title="Robert of Hesbaye">Robert of Hesbaye</a> (d. 807) as their first secured ancestor and he is believed to be a direct male descendant of Charibert de Haspengau (c. 555–636). Should this be true, only the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_House_of_Japan" title="Imperial House of Japan">Imperial House of Japan</a> would outmatch the Bourbon's age, being reliably documented - as a ruling house already - from about 540. The <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hesse" title="House of Hesse">House of Hesse</a> traces its line back to 841, the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Welf" title="House of Welf">House of Welf-Este</a> and the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Wettin" title="House of Wettin">House of Wettin</a> are both emerging in the 10th century (and so do some Italian non-ruling houses like the <a href="/wiki/Caetani" title="Caetani">Caetani</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Massimo_family" title="Massimo family">Massimo family</a>), whereas most of the other ruling families of Europe only turn up to the light of history after the year 1000.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Grand_Duchy_of_Luxembourg">Grand Duchy of Luxembourg</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Bourbon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Grand Duchy of Luxembourg">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Grand_Dukes_of_Luxembourg">Grand Dukes of Luxembourg</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Bourbon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Grand Dukes of Luxembourg">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Dates indicate reigns, not lifetimes.</p>

</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_significant_Bourbon_titles">Other significant Bourbon titles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Bourbon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Other significant Bourbon titles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Bourbon" title="Duke of Bourbon">Dukes of Bourbon</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duke_of_Montpensier" title="Duke of Montpensier">Montpensier</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duke_of_Vend%C3%B4me" title="Duke of Vendôme">Vendôme</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duke_of_Anjou" title="Duke of Anjou">Anjou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Two_Sicilies" title="Kingdom of the Two Sicilies">Kings of the Two Sicilies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Parma" title="Duke of Parma">Dukes of Parma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Duke of Orléans">Dukes of Orléans</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Heads_of_the_Brazilian_Imperial_House" title="List of Heads of the Brazilian Imperial House">Princes of Orléans and Braganza</a></li>
