<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Surnames_used">Surnames used</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Bourbon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Surnames used">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Officially, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_of_France" title="King of France">King of France</a> had no family name. A prince with the rank of <i><a href="/wiki/Fils_de_France" title="Fils de France">fils de France</a></i> (Son of France) is surnamed "<i>de France</i>"; all the male-line descendants of each <i>fils de France</i>, however, took his main title (whether an <a href="/wiki/Appanage" title="Appanage">appanage</a> or a <a href="/wiki/Courtesy_title" title="Courtesy title">courtesy title</a>) as their family or last name. However, when <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis_XVI" title="Louis XVI">Louis XVI</a> was put on trial and later "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guillotined" title="Guillotined">guillotined</a>" (executed) by the revolutionaries <a href="/wiki/National_Convention" title="National Convention">National Convention</a> in France in 1793, they somewhat contemptously referred to him in written documents and spoken address as "Citizen Louis Capet" as if a "commoner" (referring back to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medieval" title="Medieval">Medieval</a> origins of the Bourbon Dynasty's name and referring to <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Capet" title="Hugh Capet">Hugh Capet</a>, founder of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capetian_Dynasty" title="Capetian Dynasty">Capetian Dynasty</a>).</p>
<p>Members of the House of Bourbon-Condé and its cadet branches, which never ascended to the throne, used the surname "de Bourbon" until their extinction in 1830.</p>
<p>The daughters of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gaston,_Duke_of_Orleans" title="Gaston, Duke of Orleans">Gaston, Duke of Orleans</a>, were the first members of the House of Bourbon since the accession of Henry IV to take their surname from the appanage of their father (d'Orleans). Gaston died without a male heir; his titles reverted to the crown. It was given to his nephew, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippe_I,_Duke_of_Orleans" title="Philippe I, Duke of Orleans">Philippe I, Duke of Orleans</a>, brother of Louis XIV, whose descendants still bear the surname.</p>
<p>When Philippe, grandson of Louis XIV, became King of Spain as <a href="/wiki/Philip_V_of_Spain" title="Philip V of Spain">Philip V</a>, he gave up his French titles. As a Son of France, his actual surname was "de France". However, since that surname was not heritable for descendants of rank lower than Son of France, and since Philippe had already given up his French titles, his descendants simply took the name of their royal house as their surname ("de Bourbon", rendered in Spanish as "de Borbón").</p>
<p>The children of Philippe's brother, <a href="/wiki/Charles,_Duke_of_Berry_(1686%E2%80%931714)" title="Charles, Duke of Berry (1686–1714)">Charles, Duke of Berry</a> (all of whom died in infancy), were given the surname "d'Alencon". He was Duke of Berry only <a href="/wiki/Courtesy_title" title="Courtesy title">in name</a>, so the surname of his children was taken from his first substantial duchy.</p>
<p>The children of Charles Philippe, Count of Artois, brother of Louis XVI, were surnamed "d'Artois". When Charles succeeded to the throne as <a href="/wiki/Charles_X_of_France" title="Charles X of France">Charles X</a>, his son <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis_Antoine,_Duke_of_Angouleme" title="Louis Antoine, Duke of Angouleme">Louis Antoine</a> became a Son of France, with the corresponding change in surname. His grandson, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henry,_Count_of_Chambord" title="Henry, Count of Chambord">Henri d'Artois</a>, being merely a Grandson of France, would use the surname until his death.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Family_trees">Family trees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Bourbon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Family trees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kings_of_France_family_tree" title="Kings of France family tree">French kings family tree</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monarchs_of_Spain_family_tree" title="Monarchs of Spain family tree">Spanish kings family tree</a></div>
<p>Simplified family trees showing the relationships between the Bourbons and the other branches of the Royal House of France.</p>

Greenwood Press. p. 65. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-313-30328-2" title="Special:BookSources/0-313-30328-2">0-313-30328-2</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHouse+of+Bourbon&amp;rft.aufirst=Scott&amp;rft.aulast=Haine&amp;rft.btitle=The+History+of+France&amp;rft.edition=1st&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=0-313-30328-2&amp;rft.pages=65&amp;rft.pub=Greenwood+Press&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span> <span class="error citation-comment" style="display:none;font-size:100%"><code style="color:inherit; border:inherit; padding:inherit;">|access-date=</code> requires <code style="color:inherit; border:inherit; padding:inherit;">|url=</code> (<a href="/wiki/Help:CS1_errors#accessdate_missing_url" title="Help:CS1 errors">help</a>)</span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"The heart of Louis XVII, the son of Marie-Antoinette and Louis XVI who died in prison in 1795, has been laid to test in the crypt of Saint-Denis Basilica.(News)(Brief Article)." History Today. History Today Ltd. 2004. HighBeam Research. 18 September 2012;"<i>Louis XVII officially died of TB at the age of ten in the Temple prison.</i>"</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Durant-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Durant_5-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Will_Durant" title="Will Durant">Durant, Will</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ariel_Durant" title="Ariel Durant">Durant, Ariel</a>. “The Story of Civilization, Part XI, The Age of Napoleon”. <a href="/wiki/Simon_%26_Schuster" title="Simon &amp; Schuster">Simon &amp; Schuster</a>, New York, 1975. pp. 730-731, 774.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-6">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In French: <i>Ils n'ont rien appris, ni rien oublié.</i> There is no historic evidence linking the saying to Talleyrand. It may derive from a similar lamentation about the royalists, found in a letter by Charles Louis Etienne, chevalier de Panat, a French naval officer, dated January 1796 and sent from London to <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Mallet_du_Pan" title="Jacques Mallet du Pan">Mallet du Pan</a>: <i>personne n'a su ni rien oublier, ni rien apprendre</i> ("nobody has been able to forget anything, nor to learn anything"), included in: <cite class="citation book">A. Sayou, ed. (1852). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=LZpCAAAAYAAJ&amp;pg=PA197" rel="nofollow"><i>Mémoires et correspondance de Mallet du Pan</i></a>. <b>II</b>. p. 197.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHouse+of+Bourbon&amp;rft.btitle=M%C3%A9moires+et+correspondance+de+Mallet+du+Pan&amp;rft.date=1852&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DLZpCAAAAYAAJ%26pg%3DPA197&amp;rft.pages=197&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="http://www.heraldica.org/topics/national/sp_succ.htm#juan1972%20" rel="nofollow">"Documents relating to the Spanish succession"</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHouse+of+Bourbon&amp;rft.btitle=Documents+relating+to+the+Spanish+succession&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.heraldica.org%2Ftopics%2Fnational%2Fsp_succ.htm%23juan1972%2520&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

</th>
</tr>
<tr style="height:2px">
<td colspan="2"></td>

<tr>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd" colspan="2" style="width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em"></div>
<table class="nowraplinks navbox-subgroup" style="border-spacing:0">
<tr>
<th class="navbox-group" scope="row" style="width:8.75em">Note</th>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
<ul>
<li><span class="wrap">Louis had no children; he died aged 10 in 1795. His uncle, the future <a href="/wiki/Louis_XVIII_of_France" title="Louis XVIII of France">Louis XVIII of France</a>, proclaimed himself regent but both titles were disputed.</span></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>See <i><a href="/wiki/Bourbon_Restoration" title="Bourbon Restoration">Bourbon Restoration</a></i>.</li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
